<nav><a href="/home">Home</a> <a href="/about">About</a></nav>

<a href="#section2">Jump to Section 2</a>

<nav><ul><li><a href="/blog">Blog</a></li></ul></nav> ^R7j8ZOHj

Use <nav> only when a group of <a> elements forms part of the main navigation of your website or section. ^FLtjuZGu

Using <nav> without any links inside

Wrapping non-navigational links in <nav> (e.g., social icons not related to site structure)

Omitting <nav> for primary site menus, reducing accessibility and semantic clarity ^Am4FrsL9

<nav> is structural and semantic; <a> is functional and interactive.

<a> can exist independently; <nav> is meaningful only when grouping links. ^4PmzQ2gy

The <nav> element defines a section of the page meant for navigation, usually containing a group of links. It gives structure and meaning to menus, tables of contents, or navigation bars but does not make anything clickable by itself. The <a> element is used to create clickable links that take the user to another page, section, or resource. It performs the actual navigation action through its href attribute. ^kHA853PB
